  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3fccb46d-9719-446c-8bf5-dbd8ff76ea3d'
      });

  <span id="freeText4324721552993550855" style="display:none">« - Maintenant, assieds-toi, il faut que l'on parle, a dit l'ombre. Je me suis assis en tailleur sur le sol. - Tu as un pouvoir très rare, il faut que tu acceptes de t'en servir, même s'il te fait peur. - Pour quoi faire ? - Trouve pour ceux dont tu dérobes l'ombre cette petite lumière qui éclairera leur vie, un morceau de leur mémoire cachée, c'est tout ce que nous te demandons. - Nous ? - Nous, les ombres, souffla celle à qui je m'adressais. J'ai souri, je comprenais très bien de quoi elle parlait. » Et si l'enfant que vous étiez rencontrait l'adulte que vous êtes devenu... Drôle et tendre, Le Voleur d'ombres est le onzième roman de Marc Levy. Les romans de Marc Levy sont traduits en 41 langues et ont été publiés à plus de 20 millions d'exemplaires à travers le monde.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4470591149825104701">Le Voleur d'ombres = The Shadow Thief, Marc Levy<br/>The Shadow Thief is the eleventh novel by Marc Lévy, published by Robert Laffont edition and released in bookstores June 17, 2010. The narrator, a child whose author does not mention the name, is afraid of the night, "forms inviting himself in the shadows of the evening," and faces ruthless misfortunes at school as in his personal life. One day he learns, through a shadow of speech, that he has the power to steal the shadows and speak with them. Ea</span>
  <span id="freeText4470591149825104701" style="display:none">Le Voleur d'ombres = The Shadow Thief, Marc Levy<br />The Shadow Thief is the eleventh novel by Marc Lévy, published by Robert Laffont edition and released in bookstores June 17, 2010. The narrator, a child whose author does not mention the name, is afraid of the night, "forms inviting himself in the shadows of the evening," and faces ruthless misfortunes at school as in his personal life. One day he learns, through a shadow of speech, that he has the power to steal the shadows and speak with them. Each of these shadows gives him a secret. ...<br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز نخست ماه آگوست سال 2013 میلادی<br />عنوان: سایه دزد؛ نویسنده: مارک لوی؛ مترجم: مهتاب وکیل؛ تهران، افراز، 1391؛ در 253 ص؛ شابک: 9789642435616؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان فرانسوی - سده 21 م<br />عنوان: دزد سایه ها؛ نویسنده: مارک لوی؛ مترجم: شقایق مختاری؛ تهران، البرز، 1398؛ در 256 ص؛ شابک: 9786009876501؛ <br />سایه‌ دزد (دزد سایه ها)، یازدهمین اثر «مارک لوی»، نخستین بار در سال 2010 میلادی به چاپ رسید، و با گذشتن از مرز فروش چهارصدوپنجاه‌ هزار نسخه، در دوازده ماه، پرفروش‌ترین رمان سال «فرانسه» شد. «مارک لوی» در این اثر، با همان سبک و زبان ساده ی خویش، داستان پسربچه‌ ای را روایت می‌کند که توانایی گفتگو با سایه‌ ها را دارد، و عشق‌ها، دوستی‌ها، و روابط عاطفی او را، با ظرافت و حساسیت بسیار به تصویر می‌کشد. نقل از متن: «... بی‌هیچ حرفی بلند شدم و گذاشتم او چند قدم جلو بیفتد. وقتی دور شد، تازه فهمیدم یک جای کار می‌لنگد. سایه‌ ای که دنبال خودم می‌کشیدم، انگار یک‌متری بلندتر از حالت عادی بود، ولی سایه ی «مارکه» کاملا کوچک بود، آن‌قدر کوچک که به این نتیجه رسیدم فقط می‌تواند سایهه ی من باشد. اگر «مارکه» بعد از نجات دادن من، کشف می‌کرد که از آن موقعیت برای کش‌ رفتن سایه ی او استفاده کرده‌ ام، دیگر نه‌ تنها این ترم، بلکه کل دوره ی تحصیلیم تا امتحان دیپلم در هجده‌ سالگی، بر باد می‌رفت..»؛ پایان نقل. ا. شربیانی</span>

  <span id="freeText17943003062462152386" style="display:none">This book was kinda short compared to the books I'm used to read. When I finished the Casual Vacancy, I immediately began reading it. I thought this book would be really interesting because it's a Marc Levy and I already read another Mark Levy's book that was really great. But omg that was so boring! Actually, the narrator is a little guy so if we're not used to read books in which narrator are young, we might find it really weird. And that's what happened with me. To me, it was not well-written and it really disturbed me to see that, it was a kid who was the narrator. The lack of subtlety hurt me. I kinda forced myself to read this book, always hoping that'd get better soon. Everything was written in that childish way and when you're used to read Rowling's, Zola's, Hugo's books, you can barely like the way this book is written. Thankfully, on the book years pass and he grows up and we can see how he lives, his problems, etc. ...But honestly this book is about NOTHING special. It's so boring in every single way. I finished reading it because I began it lol. This book was ok because there were some parts of it really sweet and kinda sad but that's all. Nothing special. So, there is what I thought about this book. I may have been harsh but that's what I thought about it. I just hope the other Marc Levy's books are better than this one.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10850158139933542549">Have not heard of Marc Levy before coming upon this book by chance, though the blurb says he is one of the huge bestselling authors in France today and this book shows why as it is the kind of warm, remember the happy days of childhood, written with extraordinary narrative energy that made me read it end to end in one sitting - it is not a long novel and I am not sure it has a high reread value or that it will remain with me for long (though one never knows of course); for a similar US author i </span>
  <span id="freeText10850158139933542549" style="display:none">Have not heard of Marc Levy before coming upon this book by chance, though the blurb says he is one of the huge bestselling authors in France today and this book shows why as it is the kind of warm, remember the happy days of childhood, written with extraordinary narrative energy that made me read it end to end in one sitting - it is not a long novel and I am not sure it has a high reread value or that it will remain with me for long (though one never knows of course); for a similar US author i would say Michael Baron fits, though Marc Levy's book is quite European <br /><br />The thief of shadows is a first person narration from the title character whom we see as a lonely pre-teen first, while later we see him as a medical student; the ability to "steal the shadow of a person" or more prosaically to make people confide their deepest feelings, secrets, desires, fears, make him on the one hand someone quite suited to be a doctor and making friends easily with people, but on the other hand makes him a bit distant and harder to get really close to, as both school friend Luc - son of the local baker - and college girlfriend Sophie, a no-nonsense and practical medical student discover <br /><br />On the hand his connection with a young deaf-mute girl he meets on a seaside holiday and to whom he communicates by making and flying kites turns out to be much deeper...<br /><br />Anyway, this is a book to read and enjoy especially if you want a warm, happy but not too cloyingly sweet read </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2123592961248276796">*Note: Read the Chinese Edition<br/><br/>THIS BOOK. It was actually much better than I expected. I read a translation of the original (French), yet nonetheless, it was beautiful. Recommended to me countless times by a friend (who is sadly not on Goodreads), I finally decided to pick it up last summer. The experience took me by surprise.<br/><br/><b> PLOT: </b> This is a coming-of-age story following the footsteps of a young boy who discovers he has a special ability: steal other people's shadows and learn their secrets. A</span>
  <span id="freeText2123592961248276796" style="display:none">*Note: Read the Chinese Edition<br /><br />THIS BOOK. It was actually much better than I expected. I read a translation of the original (French), yet nonetheless, it was beautiful. Recommended to me countless times by a friend (who is sadly not on Goodreads), I finally decided to pick it up last summer. The experience took me by surprise.<br /><br /><b> PLOT: </b> This is a coming-of-age story following the footsteps of a young boy who discovers he has a special ability: steal other people's shadows and learn their secrets. As he realizes hi capabilities, he slowly learns to use the gift, which helped him navigate life in terms of first love and when he's older, friendships in a medical school. <br /><br />A heartwarming and moving story, I recommend it for a light read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2123592961248276796" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2616726890" />
    <a title="Parisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78834612-parisa"><img alt="Parisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547188381p2/78834612.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2616726890?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Parisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Parisa" href="/user/show/78834612-parisa">Parisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9782266216760" href="/book/show/10897958-le-voleur-d-ombres">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78834612-parisa?shelf=french">french</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2616726890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13702457352660950093">It is hard to explain my opinion about this book, the best words could be simple, impressive and full of emotions. <br/>The first part of the book is so impressive, a little boy who is able to talk to shadows and discover the real life of people around him. He has a big heart with pure sentiments and tries to help others find the right paths. The second part starts with up and downs and in some parts, less attractive in some parts until the trip to the beach where a great change has occurred to him. </span>
  <span id="freeText13702457352660950093" style="display:none">It is hard to explain my opinion about this book, the best words could be simple, impressive and full of emotions. <br />The first part of the book is so impressive, a little boy who is able to talk to shadows and discover the real life of people around him. He has a big heart with pure sentiments and tries to help others find the right paths. The second part starts with up and downs and in some parts, less attractive in some parts until the trip to the beach where a great change has occurred to him. The last pages of the book make me feel extremely emotional. I believe the writer has a skillful pen in describing the deepest emotions of human beings.<br /><br />***************************<br /><br />Il est un peu difficile de trouver les bons mots pour décrire ce livre. Peut-être que je pourrai dire que le livre est simple, touchant et plein de sentiments. <br />Le fils de cette histoire est différent d’autres enfants. Il peut parler avec les ombres et comprendre les histoires inédites. Ses années d’enfance étaient passées avec plusieurs souvenirs. Il avait des éclats dans son cœur quand son père les a quittés ou quand il a rencontré une fille qui s’appelait Cléa. Comme le voleur d’ombres, il pouvait trouver la vérité de la vie de Marqués et son meilleur ami Luc, il pouvait aider Yves de changer l’horizon de sa vie et comprenait la raison pour laquelle son père les a quittés comme il a expliqué:<br /><i>
  <blockquote> L'amour, c'est peut-etre comme une ombre; quelqu'un le piétine et part avec. Peut-etre que trop de lumière c'est dangereux pour l'amour, ou alors c'est le contraire, sans lumière, l'ombre d'un amour s'efface et finit par s'en aller.</blockquote>
</i> Quelques années plus tard, il est devenu un médecin, encore communiquait avec les ombres, il a essayé de remplier des éclats de son cœur. <br />A mon avis, la première partie du livre était attirante. Un petit fils avec un grand cœur et sentiment sincère qui vaudrait aider les autres, qui comprenait les douleurs d’humanité. Deuxième partie est commencée moins intéressante que la première. Je pensais toujours qu’il y avait les problèmes dans sa relation avec Sophie en même temps que Luc a éprouvé sa relation amicale. Je crois que l’ambiance a changé après avoir voyagé au bord de la mer:<br /><i>
  <blockquote> Il est des petites choses que l'on laisse derrière soi, des moments de vie ancrés dans la poussiére du temps.</blockquote>
</i> <br />J’ai des émotions sur les dernières pages comme je ne l'éxpérience jamais. Marc Levy a un stylo habillé pour exprimer les émotions profondes des êtres humains.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13702457352660950093" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4253931735783089370">*wipes away the tears*<br/>So... where should I begin with this book? First of all - at the moment this book is definitely the best book or best to second that I have read (can`t ignore "Outlander" now can we?). Yes, it`s very short - about 200 pages but my oh my - you get more action, emotions and thoughts from these 200 pages than you get from some 400 page book. I enjoyed every second of this book and I`m secretly wishing that the author would write a sequel to it. Yet on another hand - it was lef</span>
  <span id="freeText4253931735783089370" style="display:none">*wipes away the tears*<br />So... where should I begin with this book? First of all - at the moment this book is definitely the best book or best to second that I have read (can`t ignore "Outlander" now can we?). Yes, it`s very short - about 200 pages but my oh my - you get more action, emotions and thoughts from these 200 pages than you get from some 400 page book. I enjoyed every second of this book and I`m secretly wishing that the author would write a sequel to it. Yet on another hand - it was left off with this bittersweet feeling that you just don`t want to ruin.<br />In this book we follow a young boy, who has the ability to take another persons` shadow and see their darkest secrets, insecurities and wishes. He is scared and afraid because he can`t tell anyone and he doesn`t understand why he can do it, until his shadow tells him that his job is to help people and he can do a good job because he can feels their shadows. We see how the boy helps his first friend at school but losing him in the process. Sarcasm, right? In order to help someone, you must let them go. We see how he grows up to being a medical student, how he uses his abilities to help sick people (get ready for some crying - boys and girls). We see him helping his best friend, yet losing something again (can`t give away spoilers). After a tragic situation he then decides to help the most important person - himself. <br />This book is self finding journey for the boy. This book teaches you that you should help others but never forget helping yourself. This book will crush you. It will make you cry if you focus 100% into the story. You will see the world in a different way because stories shape you more than you know. Do not be fooled that this is a "kids story" - I`ll be damned if this is a children's book. It´s a mix of children`s, YA and adult book</span>
  <a data-text-id="4253931735783089370" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Miles Zarathustra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4095366-miles-zarathustra"><img alt="Miles Zarathustra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1280714766p2/4095366.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3094804418?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miles Zarathustra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miles Zarathustra" href="/user/show/4095366-miles-zarathustra">Miles Zarathustra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3094804418" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8740358673424821824">One of the best books I've read in a long time. A simple story with a hint of surreal, but very real and sympathetic characters. A boy grows up in provincial France, then moves to the city to study medicine. Delicately drawn mix of drama and irony. As a young boy the narrator sees that his shadow swaps places with others, and he can hear the other shadows speak to him of what they have seen... <br/><br/>We witness the pain of betrayal when his father leaves his mother for another woman, the struggle and j</span>
  <span id="freeText8740358673424821824" style="display:none">One of the best books I've read in a long time. A simple story with a hint of surreal, but very real and sympathetic characters. A boy grows up in provincial France, then moves to the city to study medicine. Delicately drawn mix of drama and irony. As a young boy the narrator sees that his shadow swaps places with others, and he can hear the other shadows speak to him of what they have seen... <br /><br />We witness the pain of betrayal when his father leaves his mother for another woman, the struggle and joys of his friend's father's local bakery competing with the big supermarkets.<br /><br />At every turn the author surprises. With amazing dexterity he maintains the various threads. I don't know what else to say without revealing the whole thing. A nod to the spirits of of Amélie and Aymé. Read it through to the end... you will be glad you did. <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8740358673424821824" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11448020611893952496">To be honest, this is not my kind of book. I bought a translated copy of this, thinking it was a somewhat fantasy-esque story.<br/><br/>Well, I was wrong. <i>but sometimes even mistakes lead to a good thing, don't they?</i><br/><br/>About the story: except the stealing shadow part, it's nothing new. To put it short, it tells a story about a boy and everything that happened in his childhood and young adult life. See? I did say it's nothing new, didn't I?<br/><br/>But Marc Levy manage to tell it beautifully, reading it was like watch</span>
  <span id="freeText11448020611893952496" style="display:none">To be honest, this is not my kind of book. I bought a translated copy of this, thinking it was a somewhat fantasy-esque story.<br /><br />Well, I was wrong. <i>but sometimes even mistakes lead to a good thing, don't they?</i><br /><br />About the story: except the stealing shadow part, it's nothing new. To put it short, it tells a story about a boy and everything that happened in his childhood and young adult life. See? I did say it's nothing new, didn't I?<br /><br />But Marc Levy manage to tell it beautifully, reading it was like watching the 2014 Boyhood movie. I don't want to spoil anything, but this book make me feel something that other stories, books or movies fail to do lately: emotional. <br /><br />And that being said, I don't really know what else to say. 4/5 for me.</span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_1912426'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1912426.Seras_tu_l_"><img alt="Seras-tu là?" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1190221955l/1912426._SY160_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LV4MN4tK3m/nF4egbD5+yqSIHyPM9l+HVB4jM05zqCDeylvqPmV6rh3+iN1D72e5nw/GszhL1YenfF6hC3kPAQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zlg3Wy6alVnO89nJvWFm4KrHqikLCzqWTkoFZEdcVXg9zGCGm7UxmDQa1rSSsH+TkUBzuf+2sJa9KHj2AlbyWQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/61788.Marc_Levy">About Marc Levy</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14794503578136531132">Marc Levy was born in France. When he turned eighteen, he joined the Red Cross, where he spent the next six years. In 1983, he created a computer graphics company based in France and the United States. Six years later, he co-founded an interior design and planning company with two friends; the company soon became one of the leading architecture firms in France.<br/><br/>At thirty-seven, Marc Levy wrote a st</span>
  <span id="freeText14794503578136531132" style="display:none">Marc Levy was born in France. When he turned eighteen, he joined the Red Cross, where he spent the next six years. In 1983, he created a computer graphics company based in France and the United States. Six years later, he co-founded an interior design and planning company with two friends; the company soon became one of the leading architecture firms in France.<br /><br />At thirty-seven, Marc Levy wrote a story for the man that his son would grow up to be. In early 1999, his sister, a screenwriter (now a film director), encouraged him to send the manuscript to a French publisher, who immediately decided to publish If Only It Were True. Before it was published, Steven Spielberg (Dreamworks) acquired film rights to the novel. The movie, Just like Heaven, starring Reese Witherspoon and Mark Ruffalo, was a #1 box office hit in America in 2005.<br /><br />After If Only It Were True, Marc Levy began writing full-time. Since then, he has written 18 novels. His work has been translated into 49 languages and has sold over 40 million copies worldwide. <br /><br />In addition, Marc Levy has directed a short movie, written short stories and song lyrics for various artists, including Johnny Hallyday.<br /><br />Le Figaro newspaper recently commissioned a nationwide poll asking the French to rank their favorite author: Marc Levy and Victor Hugo were #1.<br /><br />Marc Levy currently lives in New York City. Readers can learn more about him and follow his work on <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.marclevy.info">www.marclevy.info</a> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14794503578136531132" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;C'est drôlement dangereux de s'attacher à quelqu'un. C'est incroyable ce que ça peut faire mal. Rien que la peur de perdre l'autre est douloureuse.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/322205-c-est-dr-lement-dangereux-de-s-attacher-quelqu-un-c-est-incroyable-ce">44 likes</a>

            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Il est des petites choses que l'on laisse derrière soi, des moments de vie ancrés dans la poussière du temps. On peut tenter de les ignorer, mais ces petits riens mis bout à bout forment une chaîne qui vous raccroche au passé.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
